  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_12b19a4f-ca8b-4d68-b81c-304f5fc101c5'
      });

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <span id="freeText8255444977756330767" style="display:none"><i>Why be the sheep, when you can be the wolf?</i><br /><br />Seventeen-year-old Ismae escapes from the brutality of an arranged marriage into the sanctuary of the convent of St. Mortain, where the sisters still serve the gods of old. Here she learns that the god of Death Himself has blessed her with dangerous gifts—and a violent destiny. If she chooses to stay at the convent, she will be trained as an assassin and serve as a handmaiden to Death. To claim her new life, she must destroy the lives of others.<br /><br />Ismae’s most important assignment takes her straight into the high court of Brittany—where she finds herself woefully under prepared—not only for the deadly games of intrigue and treason, but for the impossible choices she must make. For how can she deliver Death’s vengeance upon a target who, against her will, has stolen her heart?</span>

<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/238054-so-i-ve-read-this-book-and-reallllllyyyyy">So I&#39;ve read this book, and reallllllyyyyy liked it, but then i saw the next book was in a different perspective, and so i dont know if i should read the second book or not. Please help!?!!!!</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_238054'><a id="like_count_community_question_238054" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/238054?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">6 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F9565548-grave-mercy">like</a></span>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/37981663-natalie"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_100x100-6433b08cbe793211f55e184d39e84c4d.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/37981663-natalie">Natalie</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">All three books are from the perspective of the different girls: Ismae narrates Grave Mercy, Sybella narrates Dark Triumph, and Annith narrates Mortal<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">All three books are from the perspective of the different girls: Ismae narrates Grave Mercy, Sybella narrates Dark Triumph, and Annith narrates Mortal Heart. Though I haven't read the third book yet, I have read the second one and I think that it's even better than the first. Ismae and Duval still show up in Dark Triumph, but the story focuses more on Sybella and Beast. It may be darker than the first, but it's also very powerful and gripping, and I love how the relationships between Sybella and the rest of the characters (especially with Beast, Ismae, and the Abbess) are shown. So I encourage you to go ahead and read it! <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div id="review_1163048581" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1163048581" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1163048581?book_show_action=true">Jan 09, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=plotting">plotting</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=assassins">assassins</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=kick-ass-heroine">kick-ass-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=secrets">secrets</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=smart-heroine">smart-heroine</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1163048581" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15463212668625459538"> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1420877754ra/13284811.gif' width='400' height='230' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><strong>
  <em>‘‘So,’’ she says, looking back at me. ‘‘You are well equipped for our service.’’</em>
</strong><br/><strong>
  <em> ‘‘Which is?’’</em>
</strong><br/><strong>
  <em> ‘‘We kill people.’’</em>
</strong><br/><br/>Everything in this fantasy book approaches perfection.<br/><br/>Maybe I have been bewitched, compelled, but, when I think of this novel, the word ‘‘masterpiece’’ is the first one that comes to my mind. Historical and fantasy make delightful mélanges when the two of them are present in a novel. The story may not have been of the same rare quality as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7171637.Clockwork_Angel__The_Infernal_Devices___1_' title='Clockwork Angel (The Infernal Devices, #1) by Cassandra Clare' rel='nofollow noopener'>Clockwork Angel</a>, for example, bu</span>
  <span id="freeText15463212668625459538" style="display:none"> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1420877754ra/13284811.gif" width="400" height="230" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><strong>
  <em>‘‘So,’’ she says, looking back at me. ‘‘You are well equipped for our service.’’</em>
</strong><br><strong>
  <em> ‘‘Which is?’’</em>
</strong><br><strong>
  <em> ‘‘We kill people.’’</em>
</strong><br><br>Everything in this fantasy book approaches perfection.<br><br>Maybe I have been bewitched, compelled, but, when I think of this novel, the word ‘‘masterpiece’’ is the first one that comes to my mind. Historical and fantasy make delightful mélanges when the two of them are present in a novel. The story may not have been of the same rare quality as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7171637.Clockwork_Angel__The_Infernal_Devices___1_" title="Clockwork Angel (The Infernal Devices, #1) by Cassandra Clare" rel="nofollow noopener">Clockwork Angel</a>, for example, but there is something fascinating about those two genres combined nonetheless.<br><br>Sometimes, there are authors that make us ‘think’ and try to ‘convince’ us that their heroine is special when, in fact, she is nothing more than another lucky chick. In this case though, Ismae really was one of a kind and the generalisation above does not include <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6914204.Robin_LaFevers" title="Robin LaFevers" rel="nofollow noopener">Robin LaFevers</a>. And, when I say that she appeared different and powerful, I do mean it. For instance, Ismae's body possessed immunition againt poison. <em>No poison on earth was to kill her.</em> Also, she could talk to souls. Needless to say, no body risked outmatching her. Which was not only exciting but also refreshing. <u>I was so tired of whiny heroine that always need their knight in shining armour to rescue them.</u><br><br>I saw countless reviewers complaining about the pacing. I am not going to dare say that it was nothing but fast – since that would be a lie, but, to me, there was no ‘slowness’ really. And that because 1) I was strongly hooked, 2) enjoyed the writing so much – very well adapted to the context and century by the way and 3) in every chapter, there was something new, a different scene which made sure that I was never tired of seeing the same characters over and over again or perhaps fear boredom. But, if the story does not appeal to you from the beginning, I am sure you will find this long and endless.<br><br><strong>
  <em>She leans forward then, as if eager to tempt me with what Mortain offers. ‘‘If you choose to stay, you will be trained in His arts. You will learn more ways to kill a man than you imagined possible. We will train you in stealth and cunning and all manner of skills that will ensure no man is ever again to threat you.’’</em>
</strong><br><br>The characters, primary and secondary ones, were not always ‘unique’ but they had personality! Of course I had read about many duchesses and men plotting marriage for power and wealth, but those personages being included in <em>this</em> plot, along with everything aside – magic, secrecy and an ounce of mystery – brought the banal situation of scheming to a new level. And a most unsettling one, may I add, for I had no idea what would happen in the end and who will have to die for the situation to be resolved.<br><br>One thing I do not seem to read often about is assassins. Not because they are not at the top of my fantasy professions list; it’s just that I do not choose reads in purpose for the story to contain some. If there are, then fantastic! But if none are included, then I will not interrupt my read or skip the book because of it. I admit though that the last assassin book I had read did not appeal to me. It was <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17566814.Midnight_Thief__Midnight_Thief___1_" title="Midnight Thief (Midnight Thief, #1) by Livia Blackburne" rel="nofollow noopener">Midnight Thief</a> and, that one specifically, I stopped reading when I started being annoyed of the romance taking to0 much importance and the heroine risking to go on the path I feared she would take. None of that in this, however! Only fierce, talented and conscious of their missions assassins that might very likely surprise you were featured. And, let’s not forget, they were girls. A lovely plus *wink* *wink*.<br><br>Why this book was not one hundred percent perfect was due to Gavriel, the love-interest. Don’t get me wrong, the romance had everything I hoped for – slow-burn, love/hate – but Gavriel was a little too controlling for my taste. He ordered Ismae around a little too often. I assumed he did not realise he was doing it throughout the story, but it does not change the fact that he could have been looser with her.<br><br><strong>
  <em>‘‘What if I say no?’’</em>
</strong><br><strong>
  <em> ‘‘Then you will be taken far from here and given to a kind, gentle man in need of a wife.’’</em>
</strong><br><strong>
  <em> ‘‘If you think I am fit to serve, Reverend Mother, I will do so gladly.’’</em>
</strong><br><br>If you are a lover of historical + fantasy + romance stories with a religious vibe, then this is the series for you!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15463212668625459538" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_759937134" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/759937134" />
    <a title="Rick Riordan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25375513-rick-riordan"><img alt="Rick Riordan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442449448p2/25375513.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/759937134?book_show_action=true">Nov 08, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rick Riordan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rick Riordan" href="/user/show/25375513-rick-riordan">Rick Riordan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer759937134" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9598538932436432250">hooked me with a great premise: medieval nun assassins who serve Saint Mortain, the god of death. The novel is set in an alternate realm of Brittany, where the local gods have been subsumed by Christianity and renamed saints. The old ways live on, however, especially among the daughters of Saint Mortain, who serve as the realm's assassins, killing those who need to be killed.<br/><br/>Our lethal heroine, Ismae, escapes a life of poverty and abuse by joining the convent. Soon she is plunged into a game of </span>
  <span id="freeText9598538932436432250" style="display:none">hooked me with a great premise: medieval nun assassins who serve Saint Mortain, the god of death. The novel is set in an alternate realm of Brittany, where the local gods have been subsumed by Christianity and renamed saints. The old ways live on, however, especially among the daughters of Saint Mortain, who serve as the realm's assassins, killing those who need to be killed.<br /><br />Our lethal heroine, Ismae, escapes a life of poverty and abuse by joining the convent. Soon she is plunged into a game of intrigue and villainy as the realm tries to maintain its independence from France. Unfortunately for Ismae, one of the people she is sent to spy on (and possibly assassinate) is the first man she feels she might love.<br /><br />The novel is driven by mystery, romance and subtle skulduggery. It isn't exactly an adventure novel, so don't expect a fight on every page, but if you stick with it, it's well worth reading! I'd recommend it to YA fans, especially those with an interest in history. The closest parallel I can think of is Cashore's Graceling -- another fantastic romance about a deadly heroine.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9598538932436432250" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_293872905" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/293872905" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/293872905?book_show_action=true">Mar 13, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=coverly-love">coverly-love</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer293872905" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6518865958208557373"><a href='http://thebookgeek.co.uk' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><b>2.5</b><br/>This book is like small dashes of awesomeness randomly sprinkled throughout long stretches of boredom. Perhaps I would have been far less bored if I cared more for fantasy/historical fiction that focuses most of its energy on the romance story. Perhaps I would have been less bored if the romance had been the kind to creep up on you, so that you're inwardly pleading that the characters will get together long before they even acknowledge their attraction for one another. Perhaps.<br/><br/>However, th</span>
  <span id="freeText6518865958208557373" style="display:none"><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>2.5</b><br>This book is like small dashes of awesomeness randomly sprinkled throughout long stretches of boredom. Perhaps I would have been far less bored if I cared more for fantasy/historical fiction that focuses most of its energy on the romance story. Perhaps I would have been less bored if the romance had been the kind to creep up on you, so that you're inwardly pleading that the characters will get together long before they even acknowledge their attraction for one another. Perhaps.<br><br>However, the romance was the main player in this book and it was the kind that sprang up immediately and left our heroine instantly breathless every time she saw Mr Duval after their first meeting. I prefer a book that is about more than a bit of romancing, but I'm not immune to a well-told love story either and I can easily be persuaded to award a book at least three stars if I'd been sold on it. Unfortunately, I wasn't. It all happened too soon, too predictably, too obviously. The heroine - Ismae - is a trained assassin that has some serious man issues (with understandable reason), so why can she do nothing but ogle Duval's sexy body in armour when they are in life-threatening situations?<br><br>The beginning, in my opinion, was the best part of the whole book. A young woman has been scarred since her mother attempted to abort her pregnancy but she survived, and the marque she bears is that of Death's servants. She is rescued away from the beginning of an abusive marriage to be taken to a convent... but these are no ordinary nuns. She is trained as an assassin, taught how to fight, how to create complicated poisons to kill instantly or drag out a death for days. She is the ultimate weapon and she uses her abilities to serve the convent and Death.<br><br>I cannot deny that this is a wonderful, kickass idea. The problem was that this part at the beginning is the most action-packed of the entire novel. After this, Ismae doesn't use her abilities that much beyond flashing her "womanly charms" at the men of court in order to find out information about who Brittany can really trust in these dangerous times when France is out for everything she can get. This book needed a serious injection of badassery.<br><br>The politics surrounding the issues of Brittany and France in the 1400s could have been much more interesting than it was, except for the fact that it was used as a platform for Ismae and Duval's budding romance. There was too much talking and eaves-dropping on conversations that didn't matter, too much family drama with characters I couldn't give a damn about, too much of all the wrong stuff. Not enough conspiracies, plotting, <b>assassinations</b> (she is an assassin, for pity's sake, was it too much to expect a little more of it?).<br><br>As much as I like this idea and part of me would like to know how this series progresses, I cannot imagine wanting to put myself through another 500 pages of boredom to find out. And one last thing, I'm sure some of the phrases used in this book weren't around one hundred years ago, never mind six hundred years ago... can't say for sure, I'm no language expert, but it sounded very 20th/21st century for me.<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="6518865958208557373" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_235863969" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/235863969" />
    <a title="Catie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1886642-catie"><img alt="Catie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1385169623p2/1886642.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/235863969?book_show_action=true">Nov 15, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Catie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Catie" href="/user/show/1886642-catie">Catie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Catie by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/2467655-jo">Jo</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=for-review">for-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer235863969" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5905827722584846894">3 1/2 stars<br/><br/>I may have a few mixed feelings about this book, but I know <i>exactly</i> who to recommend this to. Do you love historical mysteries? Court intrigue? Romance? Very light fantasy? Do you love Juliet Marillier? Sherwood Smith? Do you wish that The Queen’s Thief series read a lot more like a romance novel? Then this book is absolutely for you.<br/><br/>Ismae is a young teenager when she’s sold in marriage to a much older man. Her father is happy to be rid of her, but her new husband doesn’t know that sh</span>
  <span id="freeText5905827722584846894" style="display:none">3 1/2 stars<br /><br />I may have a few mixed feelings about this book, but I know <i>exactly</i> who to recommend this to. Do you love historical mysteries? Court intrigue? Romance? Very light fantasy? Do you love Juliet Marillier? Sherwood Smith? Do you wish that The Queen’s Thief series read a lot more like a romance novel? Then this book is absolutely for you.<br /><br />Ismae is a young teenager when she’s sold in marriage to a much older man. Her father is happy to be rid of her, but her new husband doesn’t know that she bears a large red scar on her back - a scar that marks her as one of Death’s daughters. He is less than pleased (read: murderous with rage) when he discovers the mark, but Ismae is rescued by a hedge priest and bundled off to the convent of St. Mortain, the god of death. Soon she is in training to be a handmaiden of death, skilled in espionage and murder.<br /><br />This book reads a lot like a romance novel, but I really enjoyed that about it. The romance between Ismae and Duval is slow-building, believable, and pretty smoldering. I was a bit surprised when the book finally seemed to be getting to “the good stuff” and then it pulled one of these:<br /><br />“<i>Sometime later…</i><br /><br />Boo. Apparently this is a young adult novel! Which is unfortunate because it reads so much like an adult romance, and I think that it would be better if it embraced that a bit more.<br /><br />My only huge disappointment is that Ismae suffers from what I am now going to refer to as “Driven Snow Syndrome” (because I see this so frequently that it deserves a label): she’s the kind of character who says, “I’m not a normal human being with a sexuality; I’m a <i>woman.</i>” That is, until one special man comes along and then suddenly it’s, “What are these FEELINGS that I keep having? Why is my heart pounding? Why are my loins <i>quivering?</i>” She startles like a little bird every time he touches her, and she’s conveniently skipped out on the “womanly wiles” classes at the convent so she has absolutely no knowledge of what sex is even about. Ladies, isn’t it enough that men have spent <i>centuries</i> pretending that our sexuality doesn’t exist and over-valuing our “purity?” Do we have to do it too? Come on.<br /><br />It’s also a bit unbelievable that Ismae would be a competent spy/assassin/seductress, and yet have no knowledge of court etiquette, social nuance, or male-female interaction. Not to mention…she has a giant SCAR. How is she supposed to insinuate herself at court as someone’s mistress if she can’t undress in front of anyone?<br /><br />Still, Ismae completely charmed me. I love her snap decision making and wild leaps of tangled logic. I love her awakening and growth as a person. I love that she’ll dangle out of a window to eavesdrop on someone.<br /><br />I also really love the mythology: the god of death and all his forms…the <i>convent</i> of <i>assassins</i>, for god’s sake! I love that I had some serious doubts about Ismae’s “calling” and she addressed every single one. I’ll definitely be reading the companion novels as they come out!<br /><br /><u>Perfect Musical Pairing</u><br /><br />Marvin Gaye – <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=2AY118Z_wW0" rel="nofollow noopener">Sexual Healing</a> <br /><br />OMG, yes!! I was *this close* to being able to assign this song only a few months ago, but then…the book that I was reading didn’t go the way that I expected and…I had to choose something else. Sad.<br /><br />Finally, a book that actually warrants this song (or at least, that's what I inferred was happening behind the closed curtains). This almost makes up for the complete lack of visible sexytime. Almost.<br /><br />Also seen on <a href="http://www.thereadventurer.com/1/post/2012/03/ya-review-grave-mercy-by-robin-lafevers.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Readventurer</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5905827722584846894" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_297435554" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/297435554" />
    <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair"><img alt="Steph Sinclair" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457555690p2/4642710.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/297435554?book_show_action=true">Mar 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steph Sinclair" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair">Steph Sinclair</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Those who enjoy YA Historic Romance with a twist</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=it-wasn-t-all-that-but-enjoyable">it-wasn-t-all-that-but-enjoyable</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=2012-reads">2012-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=could-have-been-better">could-have-been-better</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=disappointment">disappointment</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=i-totally-saw-that-coming">i-totally-saw-that-coming</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=2012-release">2012-release</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer297435554" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8089759173765507709"><b>Actual rating 2.5 stars</b><br/><br/><i>Grave Mercy</i> started out very strong for me with its historical roots. I instantly loved Ismae and could empathize with her bleak outlook on life. The novel had strong characters, a good plot, and political intrigue. I mean, c'mon! An assassin nun?! A badass premise like that is just begging to be read and loved. So what in heaven's name went wrong for me? Why am I only giving this book 2.5 stars? <br/><br/>Well, I'll start with what I actually liked first. I did like all the charact</span>
  <span id="freeText8089759173765507709" style="display:none"><b>Actual rating 2.5 stars</b><br><br><i>Grave Mercy</i> started out very strong for me with its historical roots. I instantly loved Ismae and could empathize with her bleak outlook on life. The novel had strong characters, a good plot, and political intrigue. I mean, c'mon! An assassin nun?! A badass premise like that is just begging to be read and loved. So what in heaven's name went wrong for me? Why am I only giving this book 2.5 stars? <br><br>Well, I'll start with what I actually liked first. I did like all the characters, especially Ismae. It's a big deal for me to like the heroine since I usually hate them due to their inability to use their brains. But not Ismae, she's a smart cookie. This isn't shocking since I'd wager it does require a certain amount of neurons to assassinate someone. And while she does carry prejudices against men due to her harsh childhood, there is a good amount of character growth for her. So, gold star for her. Duval, the love interest, while initially not appealing to my co-blogger, won me over fairly easily. And for all those wondering, the "His" in "His Fair Assassin" is not referring to Duval. It refers to Ismae's god, Mortain. At least, I'm pretty sure. Lol. <br><br>I also really liked the plot and the historic features. I can tell LaFevers did lot of research and it truly does show. Many of the characters in the novel are real people and the events occurring, real events. I felt it was a nice change in pace to the usual YA books I've read. <br><br>But the good points just weren't enough for me to love this book. Unfortunately, the negatives outweigh the positives. *sigh* Another book falls short of badassery.<br><br>First of all, I probably would never have picked up this book on my own if Kennedy hadn't suggested a read-a-long. I choose to avoid historic fiction for a myriad of reasons, the most important being: It's just not my cup of tea. When I have to sit down and think about the setting, time period, a huge cast of characters I have to keep up with, political talk, yada, yada, yada... it just turns me right off. It's too much. And I don't like having to concentrate while reading for enjoyment. In this case, I liked it, but then, I didn't like it. For the first portion of the novel, I was unsure of *when* in history this book took place. Personally, I cannot sit back and enjoy a novel if it feels like I'm missing a crucial part of the story. And the time period was important for me. European history is just not my forte, so I took to Wikipedia looking for answers. Unfortunately for me, I now knew how the story would eventually end unless Levers decided to deviate from history. But at least I knew the time period is the late 1480s. Yay for me. Boo that I had to work so hard to find the answer. <br><br>Anyway, that was the first strike. The second? Boredom. Right around 40% the high from the strong beginning began to fade and along with it, my eyelids closed more often then I'd like them too. Ismae is a trained killer, but there wasn't much killing going on. In fact, there was mostly too much talking about the political plans being made to ward of the French from invasion. Honestly, I couldn't care less about any of that. I WANTED BLOOD. Then it got boring. Ismae spent more time talking about all her cool weapons, than using them. She'd go on and on about her poisons and how she could kill someone with this weapon or that poison. I wanted her to take a page from Nike.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380372807i/726162.jpg" alt="Photobucket Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>No excuses, Ismae!</i><br><br>*FRUSTRATION* What good is an assassin nun that just wanders the castle?! Do something! Anything. Do the Macarena. Sing a Ke$ha song!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380372807i/726163.jpg" alt="Photobucket Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But, I was still interested enough to continue on and I'm glad I did, because it started getting interesting. However, that leads me to my forth point...<br><br>This book was entirely too predictable. Could the bad guy be anymore obvious? LaFevers pretty much dangled him in front of us the entire novel like a carrot, so by the time the main characters goes, "It was you!" you're thinking, "It's about time." And that really made me sad because I thought, "There was no way it can be who I think it is. It's just too easy. There has to be one last plot twist." Sadly, there wasn't one and because of that, I think the ending suffered greatly. <br><br>Speaking of the ending, it felt incredibly rushed to me. All conflicts came to a more or less, hurried happy ending. As soon as the baddie is caught the book has nothing more to do then fall back on its underdeveloped romance between Ismae and Duval. That's not to say I disliked Duval and Ismae. I actually liked both characters a great deal, but together? Not so much. <i>Grave Mercy</i> spent entirely too much time revolving around the mystery and not much time developing the relationship. I think the book needed to make its mind up: Romance or plot. It couldn't have both believably, in this case. <br><br>*mild spoilers* But the part I really disliked about the book was the scene where Ismae had to purge poison from Duval's body by having sex with him. I was relatively enjoying the book up until that point. When I read that scene I rolled my eyes so hard. I mean, really?! REALLY?! She is a nun assassin and the biggest gift Mortain gives her involves her sexuality? She becomes a human bezoar! Would ya look at that? A woman's body really <i>can</i> be objectified in almost any profession! Awesome. \(-_-)/<br><br>The next book appears to be about Sybella, who I thought would have had a bigger role in this installment. The mystery surrounding the girl was thrown at the reader several times and we are given no information about her assignment. Same goes for Annith's story. I found that incredibly frustrating. I realize this is supposed to be a series and perhaps their stories will be told in the sequels, but leaving those gaps made <i>Grave Mercy</i> seem incomplete. I can't help to think the book would have been stronger as a stand alone novel instead of stretching their stories out over three books. <br><br>So, will I continue on with this series? At this time, probably not. But I would still recommend it to others looking for a change-up in their usual YA readings, especially those who enjoy historic fiction with romance and a pleasant splash of paranormal. <br><br>More reviews and other fantastically awesome things at <a href="http://cuddlebuggery.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Cuddlebuggery Book Blog</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="8089759173765507709" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1483250160" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1483250160" />
    <a title="may ❀" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/49148508-may"><img alt="may ❀" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562443036p2/49148508.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1483250160?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="may ❀" class="user" itemprop="url" name="may ❀" href="/user/show/49148508-may">may ❀</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:

<span id="freeTextContainer1142367734737203591">i finished this book in less than a day bc it was so bloody good and im offended that it doesn't get the recognition and hype it deserves (yes im well aware that it was published in 2012 BUT STILL)<br/><br/>- i dont even know where to begin, this book was a ride<br/>- it starts off with a young girl about to be sold by her father into a marriage with this gross monster of a man, but nah this girl ain't having it<br/>- anyways she manages to get saved from that hell of a future and begins her life at a convent where</span>
  <span id="freeText1142367734737203591" style="display:none">i finished this book in less than a day bc it was so bloody good and im offended that it doesn't get the recognition and hype it deserves (yes im well aware that it was published in 2012 BUT STILL)<br /><br />- i dont even know where to begin, this book was a ride<br />- it starts off with a young girl about to be sold by her father into a marriage with this gross monster of a man, but nah this girl ain't having it<br />- anyways she manages to get saved from that hell of a future and begins her life at a convent where she finds her life has already been planned for her<br />- BASICALLY SHE TRAINS AS AN ASSASSIN AND GETS SENT OUT ON THESE MISSIONS AND THEN HAS TO WORK WITH THIS BROODING GUY AND ITS ALL SO GREAT<br />- i have to admit the beginning was very brief, we barely got to see her life in the convent and then it was mentioned somewhere how she spent 3 years there or smthing and i was like <i>??my dude that was only 30 pages??</i><br />- i do wish we got to see her interact with her convent sisters more and the bonds they build bc they do continue their friendship throughout the book but its not as solidified for the reader bc there isn't any background events to back it up<br />- and we didn't get to see her train, it was just very very brief and passed through really quickly<br />- that's probably my only dislikes about this book<br />- FROM THERE ON, WE GET THIS ANGSTY RELATIONSHIP THAT IS SO SLOWBURN AND BEAUTIFUL AND ADORABLE <br />- basically its haters to lovers but they arent really enemies bc they serve the same side, they just really dislike each other and THEY'RE KINDA FORCED TO BE IN A FAKE RELATIONSHIP<br />- aaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaa<br />- (basically my new favourite thing)<br />- that along with the political intrigue, schemes, court life, plotting, secrecy, treachery, its ALL so well crafted<br />- i thought the author did an INCREDIBLE job of balancing the plot, action, and romance.<br />- as much as im going on about the ship (they stole my heart from the beginning im weak) it was sprinkled throughout the novel so it's not heavy on the mush<br />- its just every moment where they sniped at each other i was <b>screaming</b> <br />- damn i love a well written ship<br />- and then when he referred to her (SARCASTICALLY) as 'my fair assassin' &amp; 'my little rebel' i fricken went ALL HEART EYES ldjfljaFJKDAFLA I LOVE THEM SO MUCH<br />- and you know those <i>SCENES</i> where ONE OF THEM GETS HURT AND THE OTHER ONE MENDS THE WOUND AND THEY GET ALL SOFT AND VULNERABLE AROUND EACH OTHER<br />- MY EFFING AESTHETIC <br />- ahem, anyways.....<br />- THERE'S A LOT OF FIGHTING AND ACTION AND INTRIGUE<br />- im so impressed with the way it all turned out and i got so attached to the characters 😭😭😭<br />- the friendships that bloomed between anne and ismae<br />- so fricken beautiful you guys i love girls supporting girls and being happy and protective of each other im soft<br /><br />this is really a sidenote, but it was giving me so many 'Reign' vibes (lolz i didnt even finish s1) and the entire time i was picturing Duval as Bash and i think that made me love him infinitely more 😍😍<br /><br /><i> “This is what I want to be. An instrument of mercy, not vengeance.”</i><br /><br />4.5 stars!</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_203589587" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/203589587" />
    <a title="Jo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2467655-jo"><img alt="Jo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596119990p2/2467655.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/203589587?book_show_action=true">Aug 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jo" href="/user/show/2467655-jo">Jo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer203589587" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6020897208307692121"><b>
  <i>“When one consorts with assassins, one must expect to dance along the edge of a knife once or twice.”</i>
</b><br/><br/><b>Initial Final Page Thoughts.</b><br/>Well, I thought I was going to hate that... quite the opposite.<br/><br/><b>High Points.</b><br/>Ismae. Breton courts. Nuns. The coolest convent EVER. Saints. The genre (my first historical/fantastical adventure… very exciting). Death’s handmaidens. 13th century gadgets. Poison. Saints. Horsies. Beast. Anne. Secret passage ways. Traitors. Secrets. Corruption. A kiss can be deadlier if y</span>
  <span id="freeText6020897208307692121" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>“When one consorts with assassins, one must expect to dance along the edge of a knife once or twice.”</i>
</b><br /><br /><b>Initial Final Page Thoughts.</b><br />Well, I thought I was going to hate that... quite the opposite.<br /><br /><b>High Points.</b><br />Ismae. Breton courts. Nuns. The coolest convent EVER. Saints. The genre (my first historical/fantastical adventure… very exciting). Death’s handmaidens. 13th century gadgets. Poison. Saints. Horsies. Beast. Anne. Secret passage ways. Traitors. Secrets. Corruption. A kiss can be deadlier if you mean it. Chess games that could give Ingmar Bergman a run for his money. Court dandies. Soul searching. Scars. Marques. Dreams. <br /><br /><b>Low Point.</b><br />Lessons on “Womanly Arts”… really? OK. <br />Hmm, the love interest/romantic situation was…. Interesting. More on this later.<br />And in regards to this… <i>situation</i>… there was a lot of unnecessary boy-induced angst. But again… more on this later. <br />Soooo much elbow grabbing. Is this a new thing? Do men really have a thing about elbows? I’m not sure I’m on board with this new craze. <br /><br /><b>Heroine.</b><br />OK, I loved Ismae. She was such a fantastic and original character and a fabulous narrator. <br />She is definitely the kind of girl you would ring up if you were in the depths of boy despair and needed someone to shake you out of it because she has these dry observations that were absolutely hilarious.<br />Example: <br /><blockquote><br />“Are men truly such idiots that they cannot resist two orbs of flesh?”</blockquote><br /><br />Oh, and did I mention she has bracelets that contain thin wire so she can GAROTTE men who dare to venture into her web of brilliance?! And a headband full of poisonous pearls? AND a knife that fits into her corset?!<br />Yeah, Wonder Woman would be jealous of Ismae’s gadgets. <br /><br />The only thing that annoyed me about Ismae was the way she suddenly forgot that she was amazing whenever Gavriel loped onto the page. <br />Issy (can I call you Issy? No? Tough.) he touched your waist when he helped you off a horse and you completely lost it. <br />GET A GRIP, WOMAN, YOU’RE AN ASSASSIN. “JUMPS AT MAN’S TOUCH” IS PROBABLY NOT IN THE JOB DESCRIPTION.<br />Maybe you should have attended your “Womanly Arts” class. <br />She has a dagger in her booties that can kill a man with a single touch but she turns into a quivering lamb when he grabs her elbow or looks at her in a smouldering way? <br />No, honey. Just no. <br /><br /><b>Love Interest.</b><br />Sigh. OK, I’ll be fair. <br />There was so much eye-rolling in the first few chapters that it wasn’t even funny. BUT it did get better…and there were a few scenes that made my Northern heart thaw a little.<br />I think when an author wants a dramatic Jane/Rochy kind of relationship it has to be full-on romantic peril. There has to be moments where the reader is chomping on their nails to find out whether they will get together or not. <br />There were no moments like this and my nails were left intact, which is good because I’ve just painted them a lovely colour. <br />It was so very obvious that these two would get together and it seemed everyone in Brittany (and probably France) could see this, except the two of them.<br />And they are both supposed to intelligent and fiery… but they sometimes came across as quite dim. <br />But like I said, it got there eventually. I know a lot of people will love the relationship and how it develops… but I’m cynical and crotchety and I like to whinge.<br />So even though the beginning was ridiculous, it did win me over eventually and it was very sweet in an ‘Oh, my lord, I just fell into your lap. Whatever shall we do now?’ way. <br />I just could have done with more… y’know… *looks over shoulder and lowers voice* <u><b>sex</b>. </u><br />It did amuse me, though, to think of the scene in the sequel when Gavriel meets Ismae’s dad.<br /><i>“So…you’re dating my daughter.”</i><br /><i> “Um.. yes. I mean no. With respect sir, I wouldn’t… um.. do anything…I mean… um. Yes. Yes I am.”</i><br /><i> “You’d better not hurt her. Because if you do. I’ll kill you.”</i><br />*Death shares a look with Ismae and they chortle while sharpening their knives that could fit comfortably in their underwear. Gavriel laughs too…as he wets himself.”<br />Awkward.<br /><br /><b> Theme Tune. </b><br /><br /><a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=39lizUf71VY&amp;feature=related" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <br /><br /><i>I want to love you but I better not touch (Don't touch)</i><br /><i>I want to hold you but my senses tell me to stop</i><br /><i>I want to kiss you but I want it too much (Too much)</i><br /><i>I want to taste you but your lips are venomous poison</i><br /><br />I think this song has a lot of relevance to this story of Death’s handmaiden and her quest to save a duchess from traitors and staying to true to herself and her beliefs while falling in love with a… <br /><br />Fine, whatever.<br /><i>You</i> come up with a song that is relevant to a story set in the courts of Brittany in the 13th century.<br />That chorus though, it’s pretty apt. <br />Think about it. <i>Think about it.</i><br /><br /><b>Boy Angst Scale.</b><br />10/10. I think I’ve pretty much covered this in the above sections. There is a lot of simpering moments that seem completely out of character (for both of them).<br />I mean… it didn’t make me mad…as such.<br />Just a little bit disappointed.<br />But I guess that just shows how much I love Ismae when she was brilliant. <br /><br /><b>Sadness Scale.</b><br />8/10. But I’m not saying anything else in case of spoilery badtimes. <br /><br /><b>Recommended For.</b><br />People who like historical and fantasy fiction. People who are looking for a series that isn’t (overly) paranormal and dystopian but still awesome. People who are proud of their scars. People who wish they could have had a thin wire hidden in their bracelet. People who think more men should wear armour and joust. People who need lessons in ‘womanly arts’. People who would like a sassypants crow to deliver their messages for them. People who think religion needs more gadgets. People who would like to learn how to gavotte. People who only know there’s only one way to check for poison thoroughly…. GET YER KIT OFF, SONNY JIM. <br /><br /><i>I received an advance copy of this book from the publishers.</i><br /><br />You can read this review and lots of other exciting things on my blog <a href="http://weartheoldcoat.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">here.</a>
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6020897208307692121" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/284836916?book_show_action=true">Feb 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anzu The Great Destroyer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anzu The Great Destroyer" href="/user/show/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer">Anzu The Great Destroyer</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=lots-of-mushy-stuff">lots-of-mushy-stuff</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer284836916" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8902198966510246291"><br/>Ugh I couldn’t finish this. I tried and tried so far but eventually the inevitable happened.<br/><br/>I may be harsh (I don’t consider myself harsh), I may be an asshole (I don’t consider myself an asshole), I may be a hater (I’m totally a hater) but I DNF’d the bitch! And it felt so damn good!<br/><br/>I was fair though. I gave it a 100-page trial, stuck to it like the good little girl I am and couldn’t even handle it. And to think page 100 was like 35% or something inside the book. 35%!!! Imagine how much left un</span>
  <span id="freeText8902198966510246291" style="display:none"><br>Ugh I couldn’t finish this. I tried and tried so far but eventually the inevitable happened.<br><br>I may be harsh (I don’t consider myself harsh), I may be an asshole (I don’t consider myself an asshole), I may be a hater (I’m totally a hater) but I DNF’d the bitch! And it felt so damn good!<br><br>I was fair though. I gave it a 100-page trial, stuck to it like the good little girl I am and couldn’t even handle it. And to think page 100 was like 35% or something inside the book. 35%!!! Imagine how much left until it was done. I’d have to chew off my own fingers in order to bear with it.<br><br>Why did I hate it? I have two big-assed reasons. One, it’s shit boring. Two, it’s an Assassin’s Creed rip-off. And a really bad and boring (did I mention boring?) one. Now let me expand my hatred a bit.<br><br>My relationship with historical books is amazing. Yep. So amazing that I tend to spill acid on them each time I play mad scientist dress-up. And that’s a lot considering the pile of ruined books lying in the corner of my room.<br><br>Then why choose a historical book in the first place? Easy, because I thought it’s Young Adult.<br> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380370930ra/723910.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Yep. I fell straight into the trap. It was the fucking cover. Does that look like a Historical Romance to you? And I presume it’s Historical Romance since some people on Goodreads added it to the Young Adult shelf. Thank you guys, you rock. But back to my covers. Just look at it. Does this resemble any of the following?<br> <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380370930i/723911.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380370930i/723912.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380370930i/723913.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I thought so. I look at the Grave Mercy cover and I see Young Adult. I read the Grave Mercy ebook and I see bullshit.<br><i>
  <blockquote>The silence feels thick and awkward to me, but any attempt to make small talk seems equally so. Wondering if he feels it too, I sneak a glance in his direction and am appalled to find him watching me. We both wrench our eyes away, and even though I am no longer looking at him, every part of me is aware of his proximity, of the faint heat coming off his body in the damp autumn air, of the scent-</blockquote>
</i><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380370930ra/723914.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This woman is killing me. How can she be so lifeless?? She’s skipping the best parts. Does it have action? Throw it to the pigs. Is it boring? Put it in the damn book. Make it more difficult for Anzu to finish the damn thing. But of course Anzu is an idiot and will try her best to read it. Ugh!<br><br>When I look a title like <i>His Fair Assassin</i> I think of - hold on to your seats folks, I’m sure you weren’t expecting this - assassins. A huge surprise there, is it not? So as I was saying, before I rudely interrupted myself, assassins. An assassin is a wicked cool person with amazing murder, stealth and weapon skills who uses them in order to remove certain obstacles that get in the way of their happiness. A book about assassins is supposed to be murder/action/stealth/blood/brains filled. At least in my opinion. It was logical that I would expect this from title. Why it was filled with boring details and lacked action? I have no clue.<br><br>Which reminds me. Did you guys play the Assassin’s Creed games? Read the books? Am I the only one who smells the theft of many elements from the game?<br><br>First the Reverend Mother who is a female version of Al Mualim, the covenant is the creed, Ismae is Altaïr. In Assassin’s Creed they get their next target’s name through carrier pigeons, in Grave mercy they use a blind lady who reads it in chicken bones and feathers.<br><blockquote>
  <i> The Tears of Mortain have done their job well, for I am certain there is no spark of life burning behind that door.</i>
</blockquote><br>Eagle vision much? What the hell??<br><br>At least if it was cool I wouldn’t mind it, but they are running the story. You don’t ruin the Assassin’s Creed story and get to live.<br> <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380370930i/723915.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Ugh I so much wish the cover had a shirtless dude on it!! Then I wouldn’t have been tempted to read it.</span>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review284836916">

<div id="review_1206269726" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1206269726" />
    <a title="Maggie ☘" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40477684-maggie"><img alt="Maggie ☘" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591529603p2/40477684.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1206269726?book_show_action=true">Feb 20, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maggie ☘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maggie ☘" href="/user/show/40477684-maggie">Maggie ☘</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781328567659" href="/book/show/38640725-grave-mercy">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=great-ships">great-ships</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=charismatic-characters">charismatic-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=book-boyfriends">book-boyfriends</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=great-reads-2015">great-reads-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=amazing-reads">amazing-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=assassins">assassins</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=beautiful-writing">beautiful-writing</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1206269726" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10403564396404193936">*4,75/5 stars*<br/><br/><b>“When one consorts with assassins, one must expect to dance along the edge of a knife once or twice.” </b><br/><br/><br/><i>Grave Mercy</i> was such a lovely surprise! It is surely one of the most memorable Historical Fiction YA books with fantasy elements there is. I cannot recommend this series highly enough!<br/><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1412892364i/11437807._SX540_.jpg' width='490' height='270' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/>Ismae is not your typical young adult heroine. She lived her whole live under care of her brutal father, and if not for the convent of St. Mortain, she would live the rest of her life with abusive hus</span>
  <span id="freeText10403564396404193936" style="display:none">*4,75/5 stars*<br><br><b>“When one consorts with assassins, one must expect to dance along the edge of a knife once or twice.” </b><br><br><br><i>Grave Mercy</i> was such a lovely surprise! It is surely one of the most memorable Historical Fiction YA books with fantasy elements there is. I cannot recommend this series highly enough!<br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1412892364i/11437807._SX540_.jpg" width="490" height="270" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>Ismae is not your typical young adult heroine. She lived her whole live under care of her brutal father, and if not for the convent of St. Mortain, she would live the rest of her life with abusive husband. Based on her experiences, Ismae think that every men is the same and for that gladly joins the convent to be Death's handmaiden and serve His will. It is surely a batter future than the one she was supposed to have.<br><br>Ismae is simply amazing. She has strong opinions and is more than capable of taking care of herself. She is an assassin.<br><br>There are also some very interesting secondary characters: -&gt; <b>“Good intentions are only lies the weak tell themselves. I will not be caged.” -Sybella </b><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1451321501i/17527818.jpg" width="270" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><b>“It is this kindness of his that unsettles me most. I can dodge a blow or block a knife. I am impervious to poison and know a dozen ways to escape a chokehold or garrote wire. But kindness? I do not know how to defend against that.” </b><br><br><br>I was little bit sad that the actual assassin training wasn't quite shown. Ismae's life with the nuns was shortly described and I was hoping to see more of the actual poison and combat training. <br><br>Nevertheless, the beginning was very imersive and gripping. After training, Ismae gets her first assignment, which she manages with ease and no questions. But her third task is much harder then even the abbess anticipated.<br><br>Ismae gets herself in the mids of intrigues and political machinations right at the court of Brittany. She starts to question everyone around her and soon finds out that maybe, the only person whom she can truly trust, is the one she wasn't supposed to. The one convent sent her to spy on, Duval.<br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1551283393i/27126029._SY540_.jpg" width="250" height="370" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><b>“I have no better plan, my lord. In truth, I am sorely disappointed in my god’s justice so far.”<br>Duval stares at me a long moment, his eyes bright as if with fever. “Perhaps that is because you mistake death for justice, and they are not the same thing at all.”</b><br><br><br>The middle of this book was a little bit stretched. I'm not going to lie, it is not always fast paced, but rather slowly revealing, intriguing and mystrious story with lots of spying at court. You can't be sure whom to trust. The prose is also worth mentioning, as it was absolutely beautiful and well suited the story.<br><br><b>AND I COULD NOT PUT IT DOWN.</b> <i>Grave Mercy</i> has the right amount of romance - Ismae's relationship with Duval is swoon worthy and amusing from the beginning - blended with political intrigue, court life, poisons and killing.<br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1551279988ra/27125768.gif" width="390" height="350" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>If you enjoy stories set in the past, gorgeous prose and interestingly balanced romance, politics and kickass-ness, as well as if you're interested in reading about Assassin Nuns (I'm sure everyone is a bit interested in that! I sure was and am not in the least disappointed), then <i>Grave Mercy </i> is meant right for you.<br><br><br><b>“The body on the ground is nothing more than a shell, a husk, and I am filled with a sense of peace. Yes, I think. Yes. This is what I want to be. An instrument of mercy, not vengeance.” </b></span>
  <a data-text-id="10403564396404193936" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_271554989" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/271554989" />
    <a title="Kat Kennedy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy"><img alt="Kat Kennedy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537750381p2/3270188.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/271554989?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat Kennedy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat Kennedy" href="/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy">Kat Kennedy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=romance-romance-romance">romance-romance-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=to-ya-or-not-to-ya">to-ya-or-not-to-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=the-great-shelf-of-meh">the-great-shelf-of-meh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=kat-s-book-reviews">kat-s-book-reviews</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer271554989" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9817789061282838246">Grave Mercy is the improbable tale of an assassin-y murder-nun, Ismae, on a mission to rescue the Duchess of Brittany from a fate worse than death – a really disgusting old, pervert man. She’s joined along the way by a studly lord-type person, Duval, in order to defeat evil (the French), crown the Duchess, and get laid.<br/>So on the positive side there’s court intrigue, crossbows, britches untied and skirts hitching and all those kinds of shenangians. And given those facts, you would be forgiven for</span>
  <span id="freeText9817789061282838246" style="display:none">Grave Mercy is the improbable tale of an assassin-y murder-nun, Ismae, on a mission to rescue the Duchess of Brittany from a fate worse than death – a really disgusting old, pervert man. She’s joined along the way by a studly lord-type person, Duval, in order to defeat evil (the French), crown the Duchess, and get laid.<br>So on the positive side there’s court intrigue, crossbows, britches untied and skirts hitching and all those kinds of shenangians. And given those facts, you would be forgiven for thinking that this is your average bodice ripper with all it’s stripped-to-the-shift, sexy occupational hazards of the 16th century, man-rooty goodness (…or badness?)<br>But this is actually a YA novel, which makes it awkward because it actually reads far more like it should have this cover:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380368895i/721478.jpg" alt="romance cover" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <br>Look, you can’t just clean up an historical romance, put it through the wash, cut out all the descriptive sex and relabel it YA. It doesn’t work like that. The result is an Historical Romance without any sex - and you’ve just removed the one reason why I WOULD read a Historical Romance.<br>They tried to do that with that Pirates porn movie. The director loved it so much he cut out the sex and rereleased it as a feature movie. But YOU STILL HAVE A PORN MOVIE! There’s just no three way pirate sex scenes to off-put the fake books, stilted dialogue, ridiculous non-sensical story-lines… actually, it sounds like I AM describing Pirates of the Carribean – so let’s just move on.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380368895i/721479._SY540_.jpg" alt="Pirates porn movie poster" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <br>The premise was very interesting and I think the idea was most noteworthy. There’s nothing much to complain about with LaFever’s writing and stylistic choices in that regard. But it’s the plot and the pacing that is its biggest let down.<br><br>Quite early in this novel we see the plot mostly dry up and the fantasy of a badass killer-nun seems to be unattainable as we’re left with a soggy romance that never feels quite convincing. Certainly, both characters are likable and work well together as a team. But the actual romance is never particularly breathtaking or impassioned. Which would be fine if the movie had more throat-cutting and less awkward moments where the two main characters almost kiss.<br><br>The mystery is laughably easy to deduce which, for me, just added to a rather average reading fare.<br>I recommend this book to those that like the idea of assassin-nuns without dealing with the mess and teenagers who want a gateway book to the historical romance genre.<br><br>Check out our joint review of this book on <a href="http://cuddlebuggery.com/2012/04/arc-book-review-grave-mercy-by-robin-lafevers/" rel="nofollow noopener">Cuddlebuggery</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="9817789061282838246" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1347760235" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17221027053758427098">Find all of my reviews at: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/'>http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br/><br/>Upon starting <i>Grave Mercy</i> things were going swimmingly . . . <br/><br/><b>
  <i>“You would not expect a queen to wash her own clothes or lace her own gown, she has handmaids for that. And so it is with us; we serve as handmaids to Death. When we are guided by His will, killing is a sacrament.”</i>
</b><br/><br/>My inner bunneh was all like . . . <br/><br/><a href='http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/texas/houston/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1438272076ra/15688234.gif' alt='Houston commercial photography' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>But then the MC was given the assignment that I <i>thought</i> would be the driving force throughout the book, only to find out </span>
  <span id="freeText17221027053758427098" style="display:none">Find all of my reviews at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/">http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br><br>Upon starting <i>Grave Mercy</i> things were going swimmingly . . . <br><br><b>
  <i>“You would not expect a queen to wash her own clothes or lace her own gown, she has handmaids for that. And so it is with us; we serve as handmaids to Death. When we are guided by His will, killing is a sacrament.”</i>
</b><br><br>My inner bunneh was all like . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/texas/houston/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1438272076ra/15688234.gif" alt="Houston commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>But then the MC was given the assignment that I <i>thought</i> would be the driving force throughout the book, only to find out what was really going to happen was not how I had imagined . . . .<br><br><b>
  <i>“He blinks, ‘If you are not careful, I will begin to think you are enamored of me.’ At his words, something flutters happily in my breast, pleasure, perhaps.”</i>
</b><br><br>And I was all like . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/texas/houston/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1438272320ra/15688254.gif" alt="Houston commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>So here’s a chick who was raised with an abusive father who pawns her off to the highest bidder who OF COURSE couldn’t wait to smack the shit out of her as well – gets rescued from said abuser’s house before he has a chance to rape and beat her – is transported to a convent where she discovers she is TOTALLY kick-ass/immune to poison/has the ability to see the mark of death on a person/etc. – is trained to become an assassin – and then gets sent on an assignment only to become smitten with the dude who may actually end up being the bad guy . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/texas/houston/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1438272076ra/15688236.gif" alt="Houston commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Talk about a real bait and switch. It was like going to pick up your brand new blue sports wagon and instead walking away with . . .<br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/texas/houston/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1438272076ra/15688237.gif" alt="Houston commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>Grave Mercy</i> could be used as an exhibit of why YA books get a bad rap. For the love of Tom Cruise, why do authors assume young people are stupid? Talk about a story that was 100% predictable. I. SAW. EVERYTHING. COMING. From the bad guy <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/texas/houston/" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1438272076i/15688238._SY540_.jpg" alt="Houston commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a>  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> to that stupid f*&amp;^%g ending. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <b>SAVED BY THE VOODOO PUNANY?!?!?!?!?</b>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/texas/houston/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1438272076ra/15688239.gif" alt="Houston commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>If you’re looking for a story with a lot of stabby, run far far away. On the other hand, if you enjoy a novel that takes you in the wayback machine and deals with romance and intrigue in the Royal Court, you’ll be like the 95% of my Goodreads friends who thought this one was a big winner.<br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
