<div id="review_284938069" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/284938069" />
    <a title="Arlene" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1746727-arlene"><img alt="Arlene" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1347048609p2/1746727.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/284938069?book_show_action=true">Feb 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Arlene" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Arlene" href="/user/show/1746727-arlene">Arlene</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Arlene by: </span>
      Street Corner Bookers - Group Dessert Pick March
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=read-2012">read-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=ya-fantasy">ya-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer284938069" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11365688746798072331"><b> Five Solid Stars!</b><br/><br/>When I was reading <b>Grave Mercy</b>, I couldn’t help but reminisce about the life lessons I learned from the nuns I went to Catholic School with. Now keep in mind, they weren’t the skills Ismae was exposed to at Saint Mortmain's convent, so maybe I should start off with a brief comparison. <br/><br/>See, I was taught:<br/>To walk like a bird, not like an elephant. <br/>Keep my ankles and knees together when I sit.<br/>My school tie is not to be used as a napkin.<br/>Keep plenty of room for the Holy Spirit betwee</span>
  <span id="freeText11365688746798072331" style="display:none"><b> Five Solid Stars!</b><br /><br />When I was reading <b>Grave Mercy</b>, I couldn’t help but reminisce about the life lessons I learned from the nuns I went to Catholic School with. Now keep in mind, they weren’t the skills Ismae was exposed to at Saint Mortmain's convent, so maybe I should start off with a brief comparison. <br /><br />See, I was taught:<br />To walk like a bird, not like an elephant. <br />Keep my ankles and knees together when I sit.<br />My school tie is not to be used as a napkin.<br />Keep plenty of room for the Holy Spirit between me and my “male companion.” ~snickers~<br />Tear my bread with my hands and not my teeth.<br />God can read my thoughts so keep them pure.<br />My foul and sarcastic mouth will gain me no points in life. ~pbtfff~<br /><br />If you’re wondering, the answer is an emphatic yes on both points. (1) <i>Yes</i>, each of those lessons were directed at me at some time or another. (2)<i>Yes</i>, I still read romantic bodice rippers while tucked under my covers at night. Come on! What did you expect? :P<br /><br />Now Ismae, the main character of <b>Grave Mercy</b>, on the other hand seemed to have gotten a more well rounded and useful life training in my opinion. <br /><br />She learned from the Saint Mortmain nuns:<br />Stealth and cunning knife combat to bring down a man with a marque of Death.<br />Feminine artistry to lure her victims into a false sense of security.<br />The chemistry of poison making that could kill a man a hundred different ways.<br />Defense moves to escape a chokehold or garrote.<br /><br />If those were the lessons being taught by the nuns I grew up with, I'd like to believe I would not have been such a disappointment. <br /><br />I have to say that prior to starting <b>Grave Mercy</b> I was skeptical about whether I would be able to keep my beliefs and deep seeded convictions about religion and faith enough at bay to enjoy this story. Surprisingly (or maybe not) it wasn’t an issue for me at all. I enjoyed the political backdrop, the killer nuns, the historical time period, the constant intrigue and yes you heard me right... killer nuns. For me, it all blended perfectly to make <b>Grave Mercy</b> a fantastical story. <br /><br />In this book, Ismae escapes the cruelty to her father and the man she is wedded to, and is taken away one night after a brutal beating to Saint Mortmain’s convent. There, she learns the skills to keep her safe from ever being hurt by a man again. After several years of combat training, she has been molded into a perfect assassin and is thrust into the political battle between three countries that fight for power and land, where she must carry out the orders of her convent. However, when the desires of her convent collide with the path of her heart, Ismae is forced to make a choice between executing a command from her convent and doing what she believes in her heart is right.<br /><br />Ismae and Duval were a perfect pair of protags, and their story was filled with enough struggle and romantic tension to keep me glued to the eInk on my reader. I loved how their relationship developed at a slow and deliberate pace. It made their love for one another believable and perfect.<br /><br />Like I said… <i>FANTASTICAL</i>. It’s books such as <b>Grave Mercy</b> that prove to me time and again that fantasy, when done right, is at the top of my favorite genre list. I’m eagerly anticipating the sequel in this story line as I can’t wait to see what’s in store for Sybella. Awesome read!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11365688746798072331" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_301204928" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/301204928" />
    <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library"><img alt="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350750103p2/4551536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/301204928?book_show_action=true">Mar 26, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library">Maja (The Nocturnal Library)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=2012-favorites">2012-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=all-the-right-choices">all-the-right-choices</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=totally-saw-that-coming">totally-saw-that-coming</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=arc-2012">arc-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=cover-lust">cover-lust</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=surprise-surprise">surprise-surprise</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=my-flat-army">my-flat-army</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=reviewed-in-2012">reviewed-in-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer301204928" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18341078384948117761">What a pleasant surprise this was! Grave Mercy won me over in chapter one and I was unable to put down Ferguson, my Kindle, until I finished it. I always have troubles getting through the middle part of a book, but that was not the case here at all. I stayed up <i>very</i> late to finish it and I didn’t regret it for a second.<br/><br/>After being abused for her entire life by her vicious father and then married off at fourteen to an equally vicious husband, Ismae is saved by a hedge priest on her wedding night </span>
  <span id="freeText18341078384948117761" style="display:none">What a pleasant surprise this was! Grave Mercy won me over in chapter one and I was unable to put down Ferguson, my Kindle, until I finished it. I always have troubles getting through the middle part of a book, but that was not the case here at all. I stayed up <i>very</i> late to finish it and I didn’t regret it for a second.<br /><br />After being abused for her entire life by her vicious father and then married off at fourteen to an equally vicious husband, Ismae is saved by a hedge priest on her wedding night and taken to a convent where she is told that she is a daughter of Mortain, the god of death. She is to be trained to carry out Mortain’s will and kill those he has placed his mark upon. <br />Ismae is reborn in the convent, determined to make the absolute best of the second chance life has given her. She is a good and dedicated student. But when the abbess orders her to go to duchess’ court and do her best to protect her, Ismae is not very comfortable with her orders. At 17, she is highly trained in every skill she might need and she has no trouble killing any traitor the convent tells her to, but the only way to get access to everyone important is by posing as Duval’s mistress, and that is very unsettling. Duval seems to be loyal to the duchess, he is her half-brother after all, but Ismae is under orders to investigate him. It doesn’t matter that she finds him attractive, slightly infuriating, but most of all trustworthy. Mortain’s will always come first. <br /><br />What can be more fun than nuns who turned <i>You shall not murder</i> into <i>You shall murder only those we order you to</i> and <i>You shall not commit adultery</i> into <i>You shall seduce for information, but not for love</i>? Everyone, including myself, was thrilled by the idea of killer nuns, but that part proved to be just a little bit disappointing because these nuns had very little in common with actual nuns. I expected more conflict between their religion and their actions, but LaFevers chose another direction altogether. <br /><br />I really admired Ismae. Getting to know her was my favorite part of this book. I liked her spirit and her intelligence, and I felt that her actions were pretty consistent, a sure sign of a well-built character. It didn’t take long for her to abandon the victim mentality and accept that she’s the one with the power, and that she earned that power by working hard for three whole years. <br /><br />While I had a lot of fun reading it, Grave Mercy was by no means perfect. People with little patience for political intrigue will probably find themselves bored from time to time, especially around the middle. There is also the small issue of predictability: I knew who the traitor was about ten seconds after he showed up and it left me disappointed because I loved everything else so much. <br />Aside from that, I really wish Duval’s poisoning was handled differently. (I have to be extremely vague here lest I spoil things for some poor, unsuspecting reader, but those of you who have read the book will know exactly what I’m talking about.) I don’t mind what happened at all, I wish there was more of it, but the way it happened, under those circumstances, felt a little like a cop out to me. It’s like the action needed to be justified by a life or death situation, which I thought didn’t fit well with the overall tone of the book.<br /><br />Grave Mercy was much more fun than I expected it to be. I can’t wait to get my hands on the sequel. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18341078384948117761" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_531405228" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/531405228" />
    <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four"><img alt="Robin (Bridge Four)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473392517p2/14105531.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer531405228" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13137358500670151849"><b>Sale Alert 13May13 Kindle Deal <a href='https://www.amazon.com/Grave-Mercy-Fair-Assassin-Trilogy-ebook/dp/B005LVQZLQ/ref=sr_1_10?pf_rd_i=7533915011&pf_rd_m=ATVPDKIKX0DER&pf_rd_p=15eb079a-176c-40d8-b46c-c48305ef590a&pf_rd_r=47GE15274G05E32H9E8W&pf_rd_s=merchandised-search-5&pf_rd_t=101&qid=1570974572&s=digital-text&smid=A1KUURLZXZKET0&sr=1-10' rel='nofollow noopener'>$1.99</a></b><br/><br/> I read this a few years ago and really enjoyed the political intrigue and different heroine. This one is more Political while the next in the series has a lot more action. Still <b>Assassin Nuns</b> are always interesting.<br/><br/><br/><b>Original Review:</b><br/>This is an interesting YA novel as it is set in the 1400s so it is somewhat historical but at the same time fantasy. There is royal intrigue, plots, strange customs and dangerous women.<br/><br/>Ismae has been marked since birth. She is a dau</span>
  <span id="freeText13137358500670151849" style="display:none"><b>Sale Alert 13May13 Kindle Deal <a href="https://www.amazon.com/Grave-Mercy-Fair-Assassin-Trilogy-ebook/dp/B005LVQZLQ/ref=sr_1_10?pf_rd_i=7533915011&amp;pf_rd_m=ATVPDKIKX0DER&amp;pf_rd_p=15eb079a-176c-40d8-b46c-c48305ef590a&amp;pf_rd_r=47GE15274G05E32H9E8W&amp;pf_rd_s=merchandised-search-5&amp;pf_rd_t=101&amp;qid=1570974572&amp;s=digital-text&amp;smid=A1KUURLZXZKET0&amp;sr=1-10" rel="nofollow noopener">$1.99</a></b><br /><br /> I read this a few years ago and really enjoyed the political intrigue and different heroine. This one is more Political while the next in the series has a lot more action. Still <b>Assassin Nuns</b> are always interesting.<br /><br /><br /><b>Original Review:</b><br />This is an interesting YA novel as it is set in the 1400s so it is somewhat historical but at the same time fantasy. There is royal intrigue, plots, strange customs and dangerous women.<br /><br />Ismae has been marked since birth. She is a daughter of death better known as Saint Mortain. Daughters of death it seems are beautiful and have some other worldly qualities to them. Ismae’s special talent is with poison she is immune to it in all forms. She is saved from an arranged marriage and sent to a convent for daughters of Mortain. There she is educated and trained to be a deadly assassin for Mortain’s bidding. After years in the convent the time had finally come be sent on her first assignment. She killed a man that might have repented his past transgressions and was trying to clear his name for Brittany (the country not the girl). To figure out who is plotting against Brittany she must set off to court with Gavriel Duval where she can use her gifts to assess who is plotting against Brittany and the Duchess Anne.<br /><br />I liked that there were complex characters in this novel. No one was all good or all bad. Even our heroine is sorely misunderstood. She can tell when someone is about to die or sense them after they have died. Even she doesn’t understand the scope of her gifts. But she is feared as death is feared. Gavriel too is complex dutiful to the core but sometimes he goes against the norm for what he thinks is right even if it brands him a traitor to his sworn saint. The romance that eventually grows between them is sweet and takes its time to blossom. He sees Ismae for who and what she truly is and never tries to change her. I felt so bad for Anne, she has to marry to make an alliance to keep her kingdom that is on the brink of war but some of her suitors are treacherous and if wed she will surely die soon after so they can control her kingdom. <br /><br />The story was so interesting and watching Ismae grow into a bold woman was fascinating. I loved how she came to better understand Mortain and the two sides of him better throughout the book to realize possibly that being an assassin was not all he wanted for his daughters. There were some great nail biting moments and honestly after the first 100 pages I just couldn’t put it down. Incredibly unique heroine.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1083807788" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1083807788" />
    <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner"><img alt="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532688964p2/31461418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1083807788?book_show_action=true">Oct 19, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner">Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=in-a-minority-here">in-a-minority-here</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=2015-read">2015-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=historical">historical</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1083807788" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6597528455875444322"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1429018400i/14515788._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>➸ <b>Book 2</b> : <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1254658872?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dark Triumph</a> ✮✮✮✮✮ <br/><br/>۩ <b>This is the kind of book you eat and forget most of the details just after reaching the last page, because if there's a new event at each chapter, you quit on the feeling that nothing happened</b>. Actually if <i>Grave Mercy</i> is by no means a bad book, I wasn't impressed either. What surprises me the most is how an original concept as <i>Assassin nuns</i> can lead me to feel slightly underwhelmed. <br/><br/>I guess that expectations are <i>everything.</i> <br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>"So," she says, looking back up at me</b></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText6597528455875444322" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1429018400i/14515788._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>➸ <b>Book 2</b> : <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1254658872?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Dark Triumph</a> ✮✮✮✮✮ <br><br>۩ <b>This is the kind of book you eat and forget most of the details just after reaching the last page, because if there's a new event at each chapter, you quit on the feeling that nothing happened</b>. Actually if <i>Grave Mercy</i> is by no means a bad book, I wasn't impressed either. What surprises me the most is how an original concept as <i>Assassin nuns</i> can lead me to feel slightly underwhelmed. <br><br>I guess that expectations are <i>everything.</i> <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"So," she says, looking back up at me. "You are well equipped for our service."<br>"Which is?"<br>"We kill people."</b>
</blockquote><br><i>My biggest fear before starting it?</i> To be bored to death. And yet, strangely, the biggest - only one? - compliment I can offer it is the fact it was so compulsively readable. Weird right? <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1429018400i/14515789._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>► First of all, how can we <i>not</i> be interested in the original concept on which <i>Grave Mercy</i> relies? <br><br>Undeniably, what could be more fascinating than the discovery of the daughters of Death, more known as St Mortain's nouns, whose purpose is to learn an incredible amount of ways to be a deadly assassin? Tell me? Therefore I wasn't bored, but interested, hooked, even - political calculations always draw me in, and I must confess that the settings immensely pleased me. As a great fan of Dumas, I always had a soft spot for intrigues taking place at Court, especially when the Kings aren't the most famous (please stop talking about Louis XIV and Henri IV, not to mention Louis XVI). Indeed there're so many periods which have not yet been explored by the literature! <br><br>However, I'm sorry, but <b>what was this obvious twist?</b> For real, I was waiting and waiting and waiting for the characters to get to the same conclusion as me and <i>Oh. My</i>. They took their time for sure. As a result, I can't say that the mystery was <i>compelling</i>. Indeed while the writing, the details of the political complots enthralled me, I didn't care much about the big revelation of the villains' identity, for it was pretty obvious since the beginning. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1429018400ra/14515790.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Moreover, I couldn't help but notice <b>the lack of accuracy in the historical facts</b> - I don't know if that's supposed to be accurate, but in case you're wondering, that's not. Oh, yes, the big events are "true", but except from them, every character is pictured in a wrong way. Take Alain d'Albret, for example. Yes he was betrothed to Anne de Bretagne, but he never had 6 wifes (only one, actually). As for Fedrik de Nemours... he didn't exist. <i>And so on</i>. To be fair, even Dumas was known for romanticizing grandly his characters, so I'm not sure that it can be considered as a flaw. I thought I'd point it, anyway, because I'm an History nerd (sorry about that). Finally, why in the world are they travelling via Quimper when they intend to go to Guérande? Seriously, lost enough, aren't you? <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1429018400i/14515791._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Okay, I'm annoying. I stop here. <i>Sigh</i>. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1429018400i/14515792._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>✐ Generally speaking, I quite liked the <b>writing</b>, which was pleasant and flowed smoothly. But then, I must point that I have not the sufficient knowledge to judge if the way the characters speak can be considered as accurate for 1400s (I have to admit that I have many doubts, because it appeared rather modern to me). Now, what I can judge are the mistakes when French language is used. Of course it was rare - <i>Thanks Mortain!</i> - but come on, don't you think that it would be greatly appreciated if, I don't know, some French speaker checked before publishing? There are grammar mistakes (<i>"entré"</i> instead of <i>"entrez"</i>) and a weird use of interjections (<i>"mais bon"</i>, in that sentence, doesn't make any sense. At all.) One might argue that I make grammar mistakes in English as well, and it's true (sorry about that). But the fact is, I'm not publishing a book, but writing a review. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1429018400i/14515793._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But let's talk about the <b>characters</b>, shall we?<br><br>▧ <b>Ismae</b>, who has a special talent for poison, is sent on an assignment in the Guérande court. Her mission? To protect the Duchess, Anne de Bretagne, while unraveling the layers of treason the young ruler faces. In a word : Ismae must use her talent to figure out who is plotting against the duchess, including her closest support, Gavriel Duval. Well, I haven't much to reproach her, to be fair. Indeed I could understand her decisions, and contrary to some (many?) readers I didn't feel like she gave up her mind for the sake of her love for Duval. On the contrary, she thinks before acting, and if she IS long to realize some facts (DUH), I can't say that she's blinded by love, as she wonders why and who and how is right all the freaking time. She didn't trust Gavriel on sight for Mortain's sake! Yet... <b>I didn't care so much about her</b> either. In my opinion her monologues lacked of sincerity and believability, as I often found myself wondering... <i>Who thinks like that</i>? Every thought is too neat, and I never really felt her <i>struggle</i>, question - I was <i>told</i> so, but never get the feeling, you know? <br><br>▧ <b>Gavriel</b>, now. He is nice, kind, but has the bad habit to order Ismae around. Yet he <i>is</i> nice. And, you know, he is ... he IS ... <br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1422743667ra/13541029.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Well, okay, mostly <b>dull</b>. <br><br>♥ That's why even if the romance didn't bother me, it never made me swoon either, as <b>I never really saw any chemistry between Ismae and Duval</b>. As the rest of the story, everything felt too <i>
  <b>mild</b>
</i> to me, and no, my heart never missed a beat. Lack of strong feelings indeed.<br><br>▧ The <b>so-called villains</b>. Yes, <i>so-called</i>, because we are <i>told</i> that they are the villains in this story, but never really shown, or not enough, in my opinion. Take d'Albret, for example. Oh, yes, he seems really disgusting, but what does he really <i>do</i>? Nothing. To me, the only real villains are Ismae's father and her previous husband. <br><br>▧ What bothered me the most was <b>the lack of involvement of the secondary characters</b>. Indeed even if they <i>exist</i>, except for the beginning, the other characters fall into the background pretty fast, unfortunately. Personally, I'm eager to learn more about Beast (how awesome is that name, by the way?) and Sybella - Annith I don't care about.<br><br>► <b>See, when I weigh the pros and cons....</b> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1381039333ra/3935470.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>... It's pretty obvious that the cons overtake the pros by far. Now, as I did enjoy my reading still, I decided for a three that I can't help but find quite generous. <br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><blockquote>
  <a href="https://meetthebookworld.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487851828i/22057164._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="6597528455875444322" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_721722729" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/721722729" />
    <a title="Lea (drumsofautumn)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7285286-lea-drumsofautumn"><img alt="Lea (drumsofautumn)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592339546p2/7285286.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/721722729?book_show_action=true">Oct 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lea (drumsofautumn)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lea (drumsofautumn)" href="/user/show/7285286-lea-drumsofautumn">Lea (drumsofautumn)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781849394130" href="/book/show/13451210-grave-mercy">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer721722729" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12587929070104999821">Definitely 4.5 stars! I WANT TO give this 5 stars but I feel like the sequels are gonna be EVEN BETTER, so I wanna leave some space for that!<br/><br/><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“It is this kindness of his that unsettles me most. I can dodge a blow or block a knife. I am impervious to poison and know a dozen ways to escape a chokehold or garrotte wire. But kindness? I do not know how to defend against that.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br/>Now I absolutely cannot believe that it took me four years to get to this book. As soon as I heard this book exist</span>
  <span id="freeText12587929070104999821" style="display:none">Definitely 4.5 stars! I WANT TO give this 5 stars but I feel like the sequels are gonna be EVEN BETTER, so I wanna leave some space for that!<br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“It is this kindness of his that unsettles me most. I can dodge a blow or block a knife. I am impervious to poison and know a dozen ways to escape a chokehold or garrotte wire. But kindness? I do not know how to defend against that.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br />Now I absolutely cannot believe that it took me four years to get to this book. As soon as I heard this book exists, I was sure I would love it but somehow only bought it earlier this year when I spotted it in a bookstore in England. People kept recommending it to me and said I would surely enjoy it based on some of my other favourites. While I knew they were right all along – it still took me this long. Now that I have read it I can for sure say that this just hit the vein of Historical Fantasy that I fucking love.<br />Now this definitely falls more into the Historical Fiction genre for me but the Fantasy or rather <b>Paranormal elements were ones I really enjoyed and what made this novel special to me.</b> It had to be one of my favourite aspects of the story.<br /><br />I absolutely <b>loved the character development.</b> I had a little bit of a hard time getting used to the main character, Ismae. You can already tell that she grows into a fierce, strong character but at beginning she was a little bit unbearable at times. But this quickly changed for me and I really enjoyed reading from her perspectives and the things she went through.<br />In general I started to care so much for all of the characters. So many of the side characters are absolutely lovable and I found myself tearing up because of some of their storylines.<br /><br />I also really couldn't do this review without talking about the romance because I FUCKING LOVED IT. I was honestly so surprised <b>how fast I was invested in this romance</b>, I honestly didn't expect it. I thought this would just be super tropey and annoying and destroy the whole rest of the novel for me but it was the exact same opposite. I thought the romance was so well done and really nicely fit into the rest of this book.<br />I know some people find the way Ismae reacts to especially Duval's touch unbelievable and annoying but I actually really liked the way this was build up and developed. In the beginning she feels uncomfortable but does realize something is different after a while. She's not instantly IN LOVE but does start questioning her feelings quickly. I personally thought the development was valid and believable but obviously that is very subjective. I thought given Ismae's past, her behaviour and thoughts made a lot of sense.<br />I think even if you don't really like romance, it should be very bearable. It is not a small part but there is enough other stuff to enjoy.<br /><br />I also thought the <b>pacing and overall storytelling was very well done.</b> There was a great mix between action, political conflict and intrigue and the build up of the romance. I was never bored and actually got through this super fast, which hasn't happened to me in a while for such a long book. I just simply never wanted to put it down.<br /><br />Now I gotta say this did have <b>some questionable elements</b> to it but I have to be honest.. I was kinda expecting them going into this book. Knowing this was published in 2012, I knew for sure it couldn't really keep up with most of today's Fantasy or Historical Fiction that I read. But I gotta be honest here and say that I was ready to overlook that, simply because I have been wanting to read this for such a long time. <br />A big part of this story is that the assassins lure the men in with their <i>womanly charms</i>. There is a TON of attempted rape and so many vile men in this story, that I found myself shivering several times. Definitely go into this with a huge <b>trigger warning.</b><br /><br />Thank fuck for everyone who has reminded me of how much I would like this over the years. I think the <b>comparison to the Graceling Realm series fits perfectly.</b> Lots of elements I enjoyed in particular about Fire and Bitterblue were prominent in Grave Mercy.<br />I'm so excited to go into the next book now. I really love that every book has a different point of view. While the overall story of this is definitely not over, the most important parts of Ismae's story are told. Knowing that we will follow the overall story but from different POVs by other interesting characters sounds super promising.<br /><br />I know this book and series is not on many people's radars anymore but I'd highly recommend it. <b>LOOKING FOR YA WITH ACTUAL LIKEABLE ASSASSINS WHO ACTUALLY KILL PEOPLE? LOOK NO FUCKING FURTHER!</b><br /><br />♦ <a href="https://www.youtube.com/drumsofautumn" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Booktube Channel</a> ♦ <a href="https://twitter.com/drumsofautumn" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> ♦ <a href="https://instagram.com/drumsofautumn" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> ♦</span>
  <a data-text-id="12587929070104999821" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer271241365" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8426629598062038826"><b>Update 11/27/18</b><br/><br/>So, this one is a double DNF I guess. When I saw <a href='https://www.kirkusreviews.com/book-reviews/robin-lafevers/courting-darkness/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Kirkus give a starred review to the 4th book in this world</a> and make it sounds so enticing, with all the court intrigue and assassinating, I got super excited and thought maybe this would be the case when I try an old DNF and love it and have a whole new set of fantasy books to gush over and look forward to. But NO, "Grave Mercy" is still too shallow and pedestrian for my taste. Absolutely love the premise, which reminds me a bit of </span>
  <span id="freeText8426629598062038826" style="display:none"><b>Update 11/27/18</b><br /><br />So, this one is a double DNF I guess. When I saw <a href="https://www.kirkusreviews.com/book-reviews/robin-lafevers/courting-darkness/" rel="nofollow noopener">Kirkus give a starred review to the 4th book in this world</a> and make it sounds so enticing, with all the court intrigue and assassinating, I got super excited and thought maybe this would be the case when I try an old DNF and love it and have a whole new set of fantasy books to gush over and look forward to. But NO, "Grave Mercy" is still too shallow and pedestrian for my taste. Absolutely love the premise, which reminds me a bit of "The Cruel Prince." But "The Cruel Prince" was so dynamic and ship-ful, and "Grave Mercy" is dull and write-by-numbers. Sad. <br /><br />I do think that those people who missed reading these books 5 years ago and are into Maas and lite fantasy/romance, should give this series a go. <br /><br /><b>Original review</b><br /><br />I don't know, for a book that received so many starred reviews it is oddly superficial and immature. Maybe too much of a romance? Not interested in finishing.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8426629598062038826" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1414778057" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1414778057" />
    <a title="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin"><img alt="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603831478p2/17438949.jpg" /></a>

<div id="review_730950744" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/730950744" />
    <a title="Rachel Reads Ravenously" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously"><img alt="Rachel Reads Ravenously" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539149211p2/14514998.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/730950744?book_show_action=true">Sep 30, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel Reads Ravenously" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel Reads Ravenously" href="/user/show/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously">Rachel Reads Ravenously</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=paperback">paperback</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=ya-fantasy">ya-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer730950744" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2255421150291840470"><b> <i> “When one consorts with assassins, one must expect to dance along the edge of a knife once or twice.” </i> </b><br/><br/>Battered and abused for the majority of her life, Ismae is saved right after her wedding ceremony from a disgusting man and sent to a convent of Mortain's, the God of Death. There, she is schooled in the art of being an assassin and dedicated to carry out his work. For 3-4 years she is trained in many different ways to kill a man, and when she becomes 17 she is sent on her first assignment. F</span>
  <span id="freeText2255421150291840470" style="display:none"><b> <i> “When one consorts with assassins, one must expect to dance along the edge of a knife once or twice.” </i> </b><br /><br />Battered and abused for the majority of her life, Ismae is saved right after her wedding ceremony from a disgusting man and sent to a convent of Mortain's, the God of Death. There, she is schooled in the art of being an assassin and dedicated to carry out his work. For 3-4 years she is trained in many different ways to kill a man, and when she becomes 17 she is sent on her first assignment. Fairly soon Ismae is wrapped up in a mission to help the Duchess of Brittany, and forced to work with a man named Duval, who also does not want Ismae's help.<br /><br /><b> <i> “Why be the sheep when you can be the wolf?” </i> </b><br /><br />I've read and heard many mixed reviews on this book since it's publication, so I didn't know what to expect going in. I really liked this book, but it fell short of that something special that would make me love it. <br /><br />Ismae is a very compelling character, if a bit ill-prepared for the assignment she was given. Duval was interesting as well, but I never really felt as if the reader really got to know him. The relationship between him and Ismae could technically be filed under slow-build, but it felt forced to me. I wish more time had been spent building their relationship because it very much felt like it went from "I can't trust you" to "We will do our best to be together in the future" in a matter of 50 pages or so. The aboutface was too quick for my tastes.<br /><br /><b> <i> “It is this kindness of his that unsettles me most. I can dodge a blow or block a knife. I am impervious to poison and know a dozen ways to escape a chokehold or garrote wire. But kindness? I do not know how to defend against that.” </i> </b><br /><br />I'm also not a giant fan of political plots in my fantasy/science fiction novels and this book was primarily that. It was done very well, but I grew a bit tiresome of it by the end of the book.<br /><br />^^^Despite all of these issues I listed above, I thoroughly enjoyed reading this book, I felt it was a very fresh idea in the young adult genre. The book also promoted important aspects such as to think for yourself, second chances, and first impressions are not always correct. All very important themes for a ya novel.<br /><br />I am very excited to read Sybella's book next, I feel like she would be an incredibly interesting character.<br /><br />PS: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I think the fact that Ismae literally saved Duval with her magic vagina is fucking hilarious. If only we all had that ability  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="2255421150291840470" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText10331216464258977681" style="display:none">This book was outstanding.     <a title="Gail Carriger" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2277045-gail-carriger"><img alt="Gail Carriger" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1476925453p2/2277045.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1092210114?book_show_action=true">Oct 29, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gail Carriger" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gail Carriger" href="/user/show/2277045-gail-carriger">Gail Carriger</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2277045-gail-carriger?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2277045-gail-carriger?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2277045-gail-carriger?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2277045-gail-carriger?shelf=coop">coop</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1092210114&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1092210114" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6766313270896197624">The series premise: three girls from different backgrounds are deemed daughters of death and taken in to a mysterious convent where they are trained as assassins, called death's handmaidens. Each is then sent from the convent into the politics of late 1400s Brittany where they find self confidence through love, purpose, and place in society.<br/><br/>The writing: rich period color, first person perspective, strong voice, some graphic violence, modest sex scenes, excellent heroic counterparts, complex poli</span>
  <span id="freeText6766313270896197624" style="display:none">The series premise: three girls from different backgrounds are deemed daughters of death and taken in to a mysterious convent where they are trained as assassins, called death's handmaidens. Each is then sent from the convent into the politics of late 1400s Brittany where they find self confidence through love, purpose, and place in society.<br /><br />The writing: rich period color, first person perspective, strong voice, some graphic violence, modest sex scenes, excellent heroic counterparts, complex politics. Close accepting friendship between girls and women, betrayal by adult role models.<br /><br />Grave Mercy is about Ismae, an abused peasant girl, for whom a convent is salvation and her devotion to her god, Death, a redemption and a means to self actualization. Her journey is one of faith ~ learning to define faith for herself, to find faith in others, and to have faith in her own abilities and in love.<br /><br />Ismae is sent into the high politics of the time to unearth betrayal, learning along the way what she must question and who she must become. She is learning about herself as she learns about her world, and what kind of place and path is open to her.<br /><br />“Is that what my life has been? A series of trials to be passed?”<br />“You come to us well tempered, my child, and it is not in my nature to be sorry for it.<br />It is the well-tempered blade that is the strongest.”<br /><br />Ismae is a gentle almost sweet character, a fish out of water in the best sense, despite her deadly abilities. The romance that develops between her and the man she is supposed to watch is part of her own journey learning to trust not just men but herself: in her heart, in her abilities, and in her judgement.<br /><br />I adored this book. So much so that I entirely forgave it some initial world building and historical exposition. This was front loaded, once through the beginning chapters (to Ismae's first kill and the introduction of the hero) the pace picks up considerably. I wanted more of the assassin training, because I like the school aspect of most books (well, duh, I wrote a whole series about this) but I can understand why it wasn't there (or was cut out). I enjoyed the journey and the characters (even though I didn't personally relate to them) but I liked them both much more as they are set into motion, on the road and into the city and politics. I thought some of the romance was a little much ~ salvation through sex has never been a trope I latch on to myself. However, I wonder if, LaFevers is playing parody with that trope in her connubial culmination, as Ismae literally saves Duval with her body.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6766313270896197624" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1263851678" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1263851678?book_show_action=true">Apr 25, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie Monroe" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe">Natalie Monroe</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=girl-squad">girl-squad</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1263851678" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8580392864326585325"><blockquote>
  <i>"I am a handmaiden of Death. I walk in His dark shadow and do His bidding. Serving Him is my only purpose in this life, and I have let my annoyance drive that duty from my mind. I will not let that happen again."</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>Like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21414439.Truthwitch__The_Witchlands___1_' title='Truthwitch (The Witchlands, #1) by Susan Dennard' rel='nofollow noopener'>Truthwitch</a>, Grave Mercy is a book <b>I should have loved. </b> It's got an interesting historical background and assassin nuns. <br/><br/>Assassin. Nuns. I'll just let that sink in.<br/><br/>Unfortunately, the premise doesn't hold up. The beginning is the best part. We open with Ismae being married agains</span>
  <span id="freeText8580392864326585325" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>"I am a handmaiden of Death. I walk in His dark shadow and do His bidding. Serving Him is my only purpose in this life, and I have let my annoyance drive that duty from my mind. I will not let that happen again."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21414439.Truthwitch__The_Witchlands___1_" title="Truthwitch (The Witchlands, #1) by Susan Dennard" rel="nofollow noopener">Truthwitch</a>, Grave Mercy is a book <b>I should have loved. </b> It's got an interesting historical background and assassin nuns. <br><br>Assassin. Nuns. I'll just let that sink in.<br><br>Unfortunately, the premise doesn't hold up. The beginning is the best part. We open with Ismae being married against her will to a much older man. The convent rescues her and she's subjected to a poison test before discovering she has the ability to be a handmaiden of Mortain, god of Death. <br><br><b>Then we go through a time-skip and everything goes downhill.</b> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1485864511ra/21855454.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I don't mind that we skip the training, but the plot just drags and drags. Half the time I'm not sure what's going on. Part of it is on me; I put it down in December and didn't pick it back up until three weeks later. But what I can suss out—war is imminent, but the Duchess doesn't want an alliance marriage—isn't written in an engaging manner. <br><br>Now, I <i>love</i> court politics. Game of Thrones is one of all-time favorite series. Grave Mercy lacks that spark that holds a reader's interest while secondary characters mill about and talk and scheme. (A few jokes now and then wouldn't hurt.) Ismae wanders around, looking for the marque that signifies divine order to kill, and slowly falls in love with Duval. It's less interesting when that one sentence stretches into 300+ pages.<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[It also takes a long time for Ismae to stop trusting the convent. Way too long. I figured it out pages ago and it looks her look dumb when readers have to wait for her to catch up. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>But it could just be me. The writing's fine, the romance is nice and believable, and the characters are okay.<br><br>That's it, really. It's okay.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

    <a title="Giselle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5789353-giselle"><img alt="Giselle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605042512p2/5789353.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/234082567?book_show_action=true">Nov 10, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Giselle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Giselle" href="/user/show/5789353-giselle">Giselle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=from-publishers">from-publishers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=genre-historical">genre-historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=age-young-adult">age-young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=arc-physical">arc-physical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=bought-in-store">bought-in-store</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer234082567" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3824358626665779055">An unsolicited Advanced Reader Copy was provided by the publisher for review. Quotes have been pulled from an ARC and may be subject to change.<br/><br/><strong>Intrigue. Murder. Politics. What more could you want?</strong><br/><br/>Ismae gets rescued by a priest from a future with an abusive husband. The two journey to the convent, and is trained by the church to do St. Mortain’s work. But most of all she’s an assassin who is marked by Death himself. She slowly gathers the trust and respect of her fellow mentors and is finally ass</span>
  <span id="freeText3824358626665779055" style="display:none">An unsolicited Advanced Reader Copy was provided by the publisher for review. Quotes have been pulled from an ARC and may be subject to change.<br /><br /><strong>Intrigue. Murder. Politics. What more could you want?</strong><br /><br />Ismae gets rescued by a priest from a future with an abusive husband. The two journey to the convent, and is trained by the church to do St. Mortain’s work. But most of all she’s an assassin who is marked by Death himself. She slowly gathers the trust and respect of her fellow mentors and is finally assigned on a mission.<br /><br />I won’t say what that mission will be just because I don’t want to spoil anything for anyone, but let me tell you this book was long, yet I couldn’t put it down. I’m not a historical fiction fan. Probably because I haven’t read a great book that’s kept me awake and entertained, until I read <em>Grave Mercy</em>.<br /><br />Nun assassins trained in combat, and poisons, and seduction?? Now that’s a book that caught my interest!! This was a well written book. I enjoyed Ismae’s journey into the world of espionage, all set in the country of Brittany. There’s romance in this book, that’s enough to keep all romantics happy. At first it’s obvious they’re falling in love, but the readers know it, and the character doesn’t. Ismae is not your average female protagonist. She’s strong, stubborn and beautiful. And the way she hones her powers to take down a life, amazed me.<br /><br />I enjoyed reading <em>Grave Mercy</em>! Assassin nuns and girls who are trained by Death itself?? Yes sign me up!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3824358626665779055" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('NyuboRgLn+DQEUM01pPEgAE54rPfzo8GGxOWPrxee84IyY2mRt/UsIi/qJjPTRlW5OKCZUwssf6pn1tXWTW7KA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('8mXOJECX+eBq5Rw+yO1k5F/u35iKIiz+4KfoGxyXr+jNh9gjHkOysDJL95LRM7kyujW/ThnAEgZSKyVy+fxvDg==')})
  }

Sybella, having already drawn the ire of the French regent, may not be able to depend on her sister and ally as much as she hoped.
